**[02:06:11] ASHLEY:** Pike grew up in the outskirts of town, near the Bramblewood.

**[02:06:11] ASHLEY:** Her ancestors were a family of deep gnomes with quite an unfavorable reputation.

**[02:06:11] ASHLEY:** Thievery, destruction, and trickery left them with the curse of the last name Trickfoot.

**[02:06:11] ASHLEY:** Sarenrae, the goddess of healing and redemption, had other plans for Pike's great-great-grandfather Wilhand, who left his family at a young age after a dream, a dream that changed the course of the Trickfoot family.

**[02:06:11] ASHLEY:** Wilhand devoted his life to Sarenrae and pledged from then on that him and his family would live a life of service and devotion.

**[04:08:09] MATT:** Advice for first-time DMs.

**[04:08:09] MATT:** I'll give a bunch of that if we end up doing the week off, but quickly, I would say, improvisational classes help tremendously, but being able to think on your feet.

**[04:08:09] MATT:** Be open to players being creative.

**[04:08:09] MATT:** Don't always shut people down.

**[04:08:09] MATT:** It's not you against them. It can be, but I like to think of it more open.

**[04:08:09] MATT:** You can let them try whatever they come up with, but depending on how elaborate or how ridiculous it is, it might be really hard to happen.

**[04:08:09] MATT:** And let them fail spectacularly, because it makes a great story.

**[04:08:09] MATT:** Build out a sheet of a bunch of fantasy names in case they go to a place or meet an NPC you weren't expecting.

**[04:08:09] MATT:** Then you can just pick a name and make something up on the spot about it and take notes afterward.

**[04:15:53] TRAVIS:** Do you design specific things for an hourglass? Are there particular scenarios that require it?

**[04:15:57] MATT:** There are.

**[04:15:57] MATT:** It's harder to do in the Underdark.

**[04:15:57] MATT:** There aren't so many traps or timed circumstances.

**[04:15:57] MATT:** I like the hourglass for certain circumstances that have a very definite time limit, and I do think up what the challenge is, what type of skills would work, or let the players come up with creative ways that they can apply their skills to a situation to succeed, and I figure out, loosely off the 4th Edition rules, where I have number of successes vs number of failures in that period of time, and if they don't manage to do it in that time period, it's a failure.

**[04:15:57] MATT:** I think it's fun.

**[04:15:57] MATT:** It builds the tension, and the party goes, "oh, shit! We've got to do this now!" I love it. Hourglass is awesome.

**[04:17:56] MATT:** How do I handle experience leveling in this game? At certain milestones, when characters have a chance to rest-- have a breather or sleep for the evening-- then that's when experience is divvied out for the next session.

**[04:17:56] MATT:** Characters don't level in the middle of a battle, or anything, but I keep track of it, usually on a session by session basis, and if there's a moment of rest, then people can level up.

**[04:19:20] MATT:** We did this together for fun.
